  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_80c0e748-cfb9-42f5-ac83-088bdfa2d448'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/14880412-indigo-crayon">Indigo Crayon</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I forgot which book it was mentioned in, but Trent shares with Rachel at some point that Jonathan was not actually killed in The Hunt. They ran him do<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I forgot which book it was mentioned in, but Trent shares with Rachel at some point that Jonathan was not actually killed in The Hunt. They ran him down and turned him into a hound. So Jonathan's punishment for trying to hurt Rachel was being one of Trent's hounds for a while instead of elf. I guess Trent decided he'd been a hound long enough to learn his lesson and had him changed back to his real form by this book.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_644894675" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/644894675" />
    <a title="VampireNovelFan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4897902-vampirenovelfan"><img alt="VampireNovelFan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1296445543p2/4897902.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/644894675?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="VampireNovelFan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="VampireNovelFan" href="/user/show/4897902-vampirenovelfan">VampireNovelFan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer644894675" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10929870342413131007"><a href='http://www.yoururbanfantasy.com/2014/01/01/happy-new-year-the-undead-pool-hollows-12-by-kim-harrison-e-p-i-c/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <b>This book is E.P.I.C!<b> </b></b>
</a><br/><br/>Let's kick this off with a few of my favorite quotes!<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <strong>"And the kiss...A tingle raced through me. Slowly my smile faded. Ellasbeth didn't know what she had."</strong>
  <br/>
  <br/>
  <br/>
  <strong>"You've had that elf as your familiar for over a year, and he's not put the sparkle in your scrying mirror even once?"</strong>
  <br/>
  <br/>
  <br/>
  <strong>"Trent leaned back, eyeing us over his scribbled legal pad.  '</strong>
  <strong>You have amazing friends.'</strong>
  <br/>
  <strong>'I need them to stay alive through my <em>amazing</em> life,' I said, and Ivy became a</strong></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText10929870342413131007" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.yoururbanfantasy.com/2014/01/01/happy-new-year-the-undead-pool-hollows-12-by-kim-harrison-e-p-i-c/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>This book is E.P.I.C!<b> </b></b>
</a><br><br>Let's kick this off with a few of my favorite quotes!<br><br><blockquote>
  <strong>"And the kiss...A tingle raced through me. Slowly my smile faded. Ellasbeth didn't know what she had."</strong>
  <br>
  <br>
  <br>
  <strong>"You've had that elf as your familiar for over a year, and he's not put the sparkle in your scrying mirror even once?"</strong>
  <br>
  <br>
  <br>
  <strong>"Trent leaned back, eyeing us over his scribbled legal pad.  '</strong>
  <strong>You have amazing friends.'</strong>
  <br>
  <strong>'I need them to stay alive through my <em>amazing</em> life,' I said, and Ivy became almost sultry as she pulled herself together in her chair and smiled at Trent."</strong>
</blockquote><br>So this is the book! It's the moment of truth for quite a few readers. Do I really need to explain why at this point? Okay, I'll tell you a story about a witch and an elf...<br><br><img alt="" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388635734ra/7890196.gif" width="500" height="277" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>With pressure building for literally a decade now, that's a LOT for a book to live up to. With 11 books under its belt, Rachel Morgan has gone through quite a bit. Her ties to the Ever After and its never-ending problems in her life continue. In <i>Ever After</i> she had to save the parallel universe from shrinking due to her faulty ley line. Now her home town has to deal with dangerous magic causing routine spells to backfire, leading to countless accidents, injuries, and pure chaos all over the city. With magic in shambles, the race relations among all species--human and Inderlander alike--soon follow.<br><br>Undead vampires are down but not quite out, so Rachel has to figure out what's wrong with the magic in order for them to restore balance before this madness leads to a point of no return. To do this will require her to tap into wild elven magic. It's as unpredictable as it is ancient, so I think it's safe to say our favorite itchy witch has her work cut out for her (the story of her life). Thankfully she has her friends and her favorite elf, Trent Kalamack, who will do all they can to help her.<br><br>So how is it? Well, it isn't just epic, it really is <b>E.P.I.C.</b><br><br><b>Emotional</b><br>I'm sure readers will finish this book with lots of feels. I pretty much went through the emotional wringer with this one, but I found myself satisfied with the outcome of the book even though things aren't perfect.  That's the beauty of The Hollows.  Rachel and her friends have to earn everything and it's a constant fight to keep it together.  We'd be in for a truly boring journey if things were too easy. Trent is not featured on the cover of this book for the hell of it. If you like him you can look forward to seeing a lot of him and his life. If you don't...you'll still see a lot of him and his life. Either way, we get a sense of how Rachel can and can't quite fit into it and he into hers. Since they are both adrenaline junkies in their own right the results are fairly interesting, but any long-term prospects will lead to a few roadblocks.<br><br>Obstacle #1: Ellasbeth, ooh Ellasbeth. Talk about baby mama drama!  Kim Harrison knows how to make this character grate on a reader's nerves, THIS reader in particular.<br><p>
  <img alt="" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384639768ra/6922655.gif" width="390" height="259" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><br>Her cute little nickname from Trent doesn't help matters. Though even I will admit that reading about Ellasbeth isn't <em>all</em> bad. For someone with so much dignity (supposedly), even she gets pretty desperate and her subtle attempts to one-up Rachel expose her own glaring insecurities.  At the heart of it, all I could think to myself is that Trent's been there, done that and bought the t-shirt, so why does she still try so hard? There are times when you really want to <em>try</em> to like her for the sake of the children, but she does not make it easy. She is here until the end of the series, so be ready.<br><br>Obstacles #2 and #3: The demons and the elves.  Elves and demons don't have the best history and our favorite demon, Big Al, loves to remind Rachel of this. On the other side of the lines, Trent's elven community is less than thrilled as well.  I honestly feel for Al quite a bit here.   He is not featured as heavily in this book as he was in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/282640716" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Ever After</i>
</a> (sorry Al fans, I love him too), but his scenes were really profound and important, further driving home the suffering demons have endured partly due to their past with the elves. I have a feeling this is necessary to help tie up loose ends in the big picture.<br><br>But even with those obstacles and that star-crossed lovers element, the chemistry between Rachel and Trent is as strong as ever and it's high time for a definitive move one way or the other.  Rachel still tries to fight it with good reason, but she's not the only one. Trent understands his responsibilities too, which should be elsewhere.  But as the great Phoebe Buffay once said:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388635734ra/7890197.gif" width="245" height="190" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388635734ra/7890198.gif" width="277" height="174" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>Progressive</b><br>There's real movement here in the overall plot and the potential future of The Hollows and Inderlanders in general.  Elves are starting to make their move, for better or worse.  Vampires seem to be taking a stand against their undead masters, the I.S. and the F.I.B. both have to get their heads out of their rear ends to work together, and even the werewolves get some time to shine.  Fans of David will enjoy his involvement with the storyline, though I found it somewhat bittersweet.  Either way, change is on the horizon for the Inderlander community and it all goes back to Rachel in one way or another.  I love how it all ties in together.<br><br><b>Intriguing</b><br>If you thought we learned enough about the world of The Hollows, think again. The use of the magic here was really interesting and the results turn everything on its head. Wild magic is really its own beast and it is a little refreshing to see Rachel try to manage something other than earth and ley line magic. It's less tangible making the possibilities feel pretty endless.  In this book the state of The Hollows in reality is not far removed from the Ever After with the fabric of civilization crumbling.  It's quite a good character study to see how people react in desperate times.<br><br>More layers of characters we thought we knew very well are pulled back, proving once again that Harrison is a master at what she does. You don't come to the Hollows for cookie-cutter one-note characters. The world and its characters are complicated and ever-evolving.  It's one of the reasons I can't quite get enough.<br><br><b>Comedic</b><br>Jenks is in top form here.  I don't think he's been this quotable since the earlier books before Matalina's passing.  Clearly time heals all wounds even for pixies because he provides some of the best laugh out loud dialogue that I've read in a quite while from him.  Of course he's not only a source of comic relief. He lives up to the pixy name by being a good judge of character and the all around voice of reason, especially when it comes to Trent and Rachel's beating around the bush with each other.  He says what we're <em>all</em> thinking. There's more of the Trent/Jenks bromance that readers of Million Dollar Baby will enjoy too.<br><br>So all in all for me this book was indeed epic. I continue to be impressed with its high quality going into the home stretch.  There are some truly amazing moments and chapters in this book that will be talked about for a long long time ESPECIALLY a certain chapter that I'm not going to mention here...<del>chapter 22</del>.  Anyway, practically every new book is my favorite since Pale Demon and this one is the BEST yet for sure! Normally I like to dog-ear certain parts to re-read again, but I literally wanted to do that for the whole book. I am grateful for my kindle and it's lovely highlighting and bookmarking features, or else my tree version of this book would be a mess!<br><br>With just one book to go before The Hollows closes up shop I cannot WAIT to see how this all ends now!! I just know that I am so so happy that this is my favorite series. Kim Harrison hasn't let me down at all and though I'm going to miss this dearly when it's done, I am 100% confident she will give this series the ending it deserves.<br><br>So, uh, should I tell you how I really feel?<br><br><img alt="" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388635734ra/7890199.gif" width="500" height="281" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*ARC Provided by the Publisher<br>*Review also posted to <a href="http://www.amazon.com/review/R19M438J1B6VZI/ref=cm_cr_rdp_perm?ie=UTF8&amp;ASIN=B00DB3DBGI&amp;linkCode=&amp;nodeID=&amp;tag=" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a>. <br><br><b>Old updates:</b><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><b>Pre-1/1/2014</b><br>5 SMEXY ELFTASTIC STARS!! Best. Book. EVAH!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380382008ra/739479.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh, and uh one of these may or may not come in handy. <br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=1dysk8" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381156671ra/4401321.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>Full review to come. <br><br><b>10/21/2013</b>:<br>With Kim Harrison's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/115190-hollows-read-along-with-kim" rel="nofollow noopener">author read-along</a> Harper Voyager is offering the books for $1.99 for a limited time while we're reading them with Kim. I bought The Good, the Bad, and the Undead and it offered Chapter 2 of The Undead Pool! So if you're really anxious for more you should check it out, though the last line of the chapter will leave your head spinning. <br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.harpercollinsapps.com/book/9780061744518/Good-the-Bad-and-the-Undead-The-by-Kim-Harrison/">http://www.harpercollinsapps.com/book...</a><br><br>Kim will be offering the chapters on her site for free eventually, but if you just can't wait, there you have it. <br><br><b>Pre-10/7/2013:</b><br>ARC available for request (though approval is not guaranteed):<br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://edelweiss.abovethetreeline.com/ProductDetailPage.aspx?sequence=28&amp;group=galleys&amp;keywords=&amp;searchContext=&amp;searchOrgID=&amp;searchCatalogID=&amp;searchMailingID=&amp;sku=0061957933">http://edelweiss.abovethetreeline.com...</a><br><br>TRENT AND RACHEL SMEX!! BRING IT ON!!<br><br>You guys know me. I typically don't rate things 5 stars before actually reading them, but with the cover reveal and what I KNOW is going to be happening...yeah I don't think I need psychic powers to know how much I'm going to love this. What I REALLY need is an ARC!!! Great first chappie too. A promise of things to come for sure!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_621141513" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/621141513" />
    <a title="Lynsey   (A Bookish Life)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5112089-lynsey-a-bookish-life"><img alt="Lynsey   (A Bookish Life)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499618776p2/5112089.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/621141513?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lynsey   (A Bookish Life)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lynsey   (A Bookish Life)" href="/user/show/5112089-lynsey-a-bookish-life">Lynsey   (A Bookish Life)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer621141513" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16771879530356849405"><b>
  <i>A Wild Magic Ride.</i>
</b><br/><br/>To say this book is highly anticipated might just be the biggest understatement I’ve ever made. I can think of no other series where the author has led readers to such an unbearable edge of anticipation, held them there mercilessly for what seems like millennia, and made them grateful for it. It smacks of pure masochism if you ask me. I had no idea I swung that way, but apparently I’m all for it.<br/><br/>Of course, I’m talking about the Trent-Rachel relationship. What else? It’s qui</span>
  <span id="freeText16771879530356849405" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>A Wild Magic Ride.</i>
</b><br><br>To say this book is highly anticipated might just be the biggest understatement I’ve ever made. I can think of no other series where the author has led readers to such an unbearable edge of anticipation, held them there mercilessly for what seems like millennia, and made them grateful for it. It smacks of pure masochism if you ask me. I had no idea I swung that way, but apparently I’m all for it.<br><br>Of course, I’m talking about the Trent-Rachel relationship. What else? It’s quite positively the most addictive, thrilling, nail-biting storyline I’ve ever read ever in the history of ever. And since we’re only one book away from the end of this genre-changing series, it’s time for things to get serious. Isn’t it? Please? <i>Please let it be time to get serious!</i><br><br>Now, you know I can’t actually tell you anything about that part of it. And really, you don’t want me to. You might be thinking you want me to, but you’re mistaken. So just put it out of your mind, ‘kay?<br><br>Okay, good.<br><br>Moving on, what else is happening in this instalment? Well, lots of things! For starters, strange bubbles of magic are cropping up all over Cincinnati, causing misfires in Inderlander’s innate magic and the spells they cast. It quickly becomes a full-scale epidemic involving the F.I.B , the I.S. <i>and</i> the vampires. So who better to tackle the problem than everybody’s favourite go-to girl, the glue that holds them all together, Rachel Morgan. Luckily, these days Rachel has several sidekicks on standby— none more splendiferous than the most recent addition, Trent Kalamack! And even better, she’s now developed to the point where she will actually accept people’s help gladly. Between Trent’s resources, Rachel’s tenacity, Ivy’s planning, and Jenks’...Jenksness, they’ve surely got this problem in the bag, right?<br><br>Well, maybe, maybe not. This might just be the biggest challenge Rachel and crew have ever faced. It’s not just the scale of it, but the unpredictability. How can they prevent something when they have no way of anticipating where will be hit next?<br><br>In usual Harrison fashion, the pacing of The Undead Pool is spot on. The story evolves naturally with gorgeous little interludes showcasing the beautiful friendships that have been established over the last 12 books. At this point, reading a Hollows novel is like slipping into my most comfortable jeans. It’s such a warm, delightful place to be, I never want to leave. I find myself watching the percentage on my Kindle increase with dismay. <i>Why can’t it just last forever?</i> <i>I wouldn’t mind, honest!</i> And to think there’s only one more book left...*sobs*<br><br>What will we do, guys? <i>What will we do?!</i><br><br>Like the last several books in this series, The Undead Pool is an <i>easy</i> five star read for me, and Harrison’s place in my mind as the leader of the pack is holding firm. I predict this book will be a fan favourite, with several sections highlighted for easy reference and dog-eared from overuse. And trust me, mine will be no exception!<br><br>5 Stars ★★★★★<br>ARC provided by the publisher in exchange for an honest review.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380422421i/840443._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>And Chapter one!</b><br><br>From Kim's blog!<br><br>"I promised you a treat today, other than this big, beautiful, cover of Rachel and yes, Trent. More on the treat in a moment. I just want to look at it for a moment and smile at what it promises, not just more Trent, but a Trent who is willing to be there, knowing who she is and not minding that at all. And isn’t that what we all want? To be accepted for what we are, proudly what we are?"<br><br><a href="http://www.kimharrison.net/BookPages/TUP/TUP.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Read Chapter one of The Undead Pool here</a><br><br>I did and ZOMG! So good!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16771879530356849405" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_864788654" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/864788654" />
    <a title="Ferdy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy"><img alt="Ferdy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487898103p2/4596358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/864788654?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ferdy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ferdy" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy">Ferdy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=abusive-love-interest">abusive-love-interest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=annoying-kids">annoying-kids</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=ugh">ugh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=awful-love-interest">awful-love-interest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=liked-the-world">liked-the-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=used-to-like-heroine">used-to-like-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=bastard-hero">bastard-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=cheesy">cheesy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=fucked-up-romance">fucked-up-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=witchy-shit">witchy-shit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer864788654" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7732873719302125407"><b>Spoilers</b><br/><br/>What the hell has happened to this series? It went from Rachel having adventures, working on cases with Ivy and Jenks, and getting into all sorts of trouble to Rachel fawning over Trent and blushing like a schoolgirl-jammy-cow-idiot-twit. Everything was about bloody Trent, his boring kids, his dull elves, and his 'oh I'm such a martyr, I'm suffering for everybody, woe is me' nonsense. Ugh.<br/><br/><b>Random, Ranty, Repetitive thoughts:</b><br/><br/>-What's what: Magic playing up and vampires going crazy and weird</span>
  <span id="freeText7732873719302125407" style="display:none"><b>Spoilers</b><br /><br />What the hell has happened to this series? It went from Rachel having adventures, working on cases with Ivy and Jenks, and getting into all sorts of trouble to Rachel fawning over Trent and blushing like a schoolgirl-jammy-cow-idiot-twit. Everything was about bloody Trent, his boring kids, his dull elves, and his 'oh I'm such a martyr, I'm suffering for everybody, woe is me' nonsense. Ugh.<br /><br /><b>Random, Ranty, Repetitive thoughts:</b><br /><br />-What's what: Magic playing up and vampires going crazy and weird. Rachel investigates, she naturally blames herself for everything, and generally acts like an insufferable twit.<br /><br />-Why has the series suddenly changed from being all about the Hollows to all about elves and their elf related nonsense? All the rest of the supernaturals seem to have taken a back seat in comparison. I'm sick of Trent, his kids/fiancee, the elves, their goddess and all that rubbish, but because the author wants to shoehorn Trent into all of Rachel's adventures the elves have taken over every story. Not impressed.<br /><br />-Rachel spent most of her time fantasising about Trent and whining about how wrong it was to think smexy thoughts about him. It was exhausting and boring to read.<br />Also, her being all protective of Trent made me cringe, she acted like an overprotective mother… Her hackles were raised if anyone so much as looked at him wrong. I preferred when Rachel didn't have such lovey dovey, pathetic, schoolgirl/maternal feelings for Trent.<br /><br />-It was obvious that Rachel loved Trent and would do anything for him… But there was nowhere near the same level of devotion and love from Trent. He only fancied Rachel because of 1. What she could do for him 2. She was the opposite of all the elf type duties that he'd been pushed to do since birth and 3. He liked rebelling against the elf rules by dating a demon.<br /><br />-I got sick of the repeated mentions of Trent's wispy hair, his clothes, his body. Also, why did I need to know what Trent smelt like every 5 minutes?! I was desperate for Rachel to stop perving on him like some embarrassing fangirl. Her whole Trent obsession was weird.<br /><br />-I rolled my eyes at Rachel's teenage reactions to Trent. Anytime he looked at her or was close to her or touched her she would blush and feel all fluttered. Get a bloody grip. <br /><br />-I hated how Rachel was overly apologetic and guilty about things she didn't even need to feel that way about. Her whole 'I'm unworthy and a bad person and don't deserve anything good' routine grated on me. Rachel has only ever done the best she could, even if she messed up, she always tried to help those around her yet she still acted like she was undeserving. Ugh, I hate MC's with that that sort of attitude.<br /><br />-Since it's obvious that Rachel and Trent are endgame it means that Rachel won't have kids of her own and will have to make do with being a stepmum. I'm sick of the amount of PNR/UF heroines having to be a stepmum to the heroes kids. Why can't it be the other way around for a change? <br />Oh, and if by some miracle Rachel and Trent can have a kid together I'll be pissed… If Al couldn't have a kid with Ceri after trying for a 1000 years then Rachel and Trent shouldn't be able to either.<br /><br />-Rachel should have left Trent to Ellasbeth, it was clear they could have made things work, Trent definitely had a strong connection and affection for her considering all their hand touching and heated moments. Rachel will now have to deal with Ellasbeth and Trent being bonded and all parenty together for the rest of her life… Yea, I'm pretty sure Rachel's immortality will vanish so she can grow old, be childless, and die with Trent. Ugh. <br /><br />-I didn't buy Trent's love or almost love for Rachel whatsoever. Whenever she was in danger, he was more worried about himself, if he really loved her he should have wanted to protect her over his own life but that wasn't the case, it was clear Rachel would do anything for him but he wouldn't do the same. Sure, he helped her now and again but that wasn't out of love it was because he liked the danger and freedom. He didn't want to follow the rules that were put on him, he wanted to be his own person, and he knew Rachel could help him with that… Anything he supposedly did for her was only out of self interest.<br /><br />-I hope Ellasbeth doesn't turn into some villainous caricature and look like the jealous other woman just so Rachel can come across like the perfect girlfriend and stepmother. Ugh, if Rachel had any sense she'd let Trent, Ellasbeth, and Lucy be a proper family.<br /><br />-I didn't like the whole contrived Rachel and Trent are meant to be vibe. The author seemed to bang on about both of them having important responsibilities and having to do dangerous things for the safety of loved ones… And them loving horses and having lame inside jokes. Their 'connection' didn't feel organic, it felt forced.<br /><br />-What was the point of Ayer being a Kisten look alike? How was that relevant to anything? All it did was make Rachel mildly angsty. <br />Ayer was a pathetic brat who put thousands of lives in danger just because he was pissed at non living vampires. So yea why did he need to look like Kisten for that?!<br /><br />-I didn't buy the whole Ivy/Nina romance. It felt as if the only reason Ivy was made to move on from Rachel was so that readers would no longer ship them and instead ship Trent/Rachel. <br /><br />-The whole ley line, mystic, wave rubbish made little sense to me. Why did the mystics cause magic to fuck up? How did the free vampires know what the mystics would do to the non living vampires? Did that elf tell them? How would he know? How were the mystics even caught and used to begin with? Why was it Rachel's ley line that was being used?<br /><br />-I found it funny that Trent wasn't willing to risk his position as elf leader when Rachel desperately needed help and her life was in danger yet he was perfectly willing to risk it all when he realised he didn't have a say in her life. So yea, her life wasn't worth much to him but the need to control her was worth everything. What a prick.<br /><br />-For most of the series Trent has done nothing but use, abuse, threaten and manipulate Rachel. In the last few books when they started to get along and have feelings for each other he still used her, lied to her, willingly tricked her, enslaved her, and let her risk her life whilst he was safely tucked up somewhere else… He keeps fucking over Rachel even though he supposedly cares about her, he only does the right thing at the very end when he's already fucked her over in some way or another. And even then he only eventually does the right thing by Rachel because he wants something out of it. He's the most rubbish love interest Rachel has ever had, he really doesn't give a fuck about her, his first priority will always be his own safety and happiness, he's even worse than Nick. I'm sure in the next book he'll fuck over Rachel again in some way or another. Of course, Rachel will defend him, be loyal to him, risk her life for him, put him first, and do anything for him — it's a shame Trent would never do the same for her.<br /><br />-David/Rachel would make a much better couple but since he respects her and treat her well that won't happen, it seems like Rachel can only end up with a douche.<br /><br />-I rolled my eyes at Ivy wanting to move out of the church and live with Nina just as Rachel/Trent hooked up. Yea, that conveniently makes way for Trent and his kids to live in the church with Rachel. Ugh.<br /><br />-Trent suddenly playing the hero and caring about complete strangers was ridiculous. He was cool with killing innocents before but now that he was supposedly in wuv with Rachel he was all about the greater good. I didn't buy the 180 character 'development' at all.<br /><br />-I got sick of the amount of times someone shouted 'no' whenever things got crazy or deadly. It was silly and melodramatic.<br /><br />-I found it annoying that Rachel's friends (Jenks, Ivy, Trent) all accepted Trent as part of their lives after everything he did to Rachel yet Trent's friends (Quen and Jonathan) still treated Rachel like rubbish even though she'd saved Trent (and his kids) countless times. It was ridiculous.<br /><br />-Why the hell did Rachel keep acting like the problem with the mystics/goddess/sleeping vampires was all her fault? It wasn't. She was so dumb to feel guilty about the whole situation and apologise to everyone around her. None of it was her problem, but the silly cow banged on about how it was all her fault. If anyone was to blame it was Trent since it was his people that started the whole mess, why didn't someone point that out? Why didn't Trent tell Rachel the mess was down to him/his people?? I'm so sick of her acting like a martyr, feeling responsible for everyone, always being apologetic and feeling guilty, and never letting Trent or anyone else feel bad for something they did wrong. Ugh, Rachel was so infuriating.<br /><br />-Why didn't Trent tell Rachel he was helping Newt with the horse? Why did he keep that secret from her? He's always keeping things from Rachel just so he can have the upper hand. The slimy git.<br /><br />-I rolled my eyes at Al no longer wanting anything to do with Rachel. Really? For the entire series he was always in her face, and in the last few books they both needed each other for various reasons… But because Al was in the way of Trent and Rachel's lame relationship he suddenly washed his hands off her even though NOTHING in the past had ever made him let go of her before. Yea, I didn't buy him suddenly giving up on Rachel after all that he'd invested in her. It felt like anything on Rachel's side that could threaten her relationship with Trent was conveniently dealt with. It was all so forced.<br /><br />-The dialogue was a little weird this time around, it didn't always flow very well.<br /><br />-Trent fans will most likely love this installment, but since I despise Trent and everything elf related I pretty much hated it. The only reason it didn't get 1 star was because I loved all Jenks, Ivy, and Newt/Al parts.<br /><br />All in all, I wasn't impressed with the elf-heavy plot, everything Trent related, the cringey romance, and Rachel's pathetic personality.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7732873719302125407" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie"><img alt="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514769932p2/3275325.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " href="/user/show/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie">Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062300157" href="/book/show/18053155-the-undead-pool">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie?shelf=emotional-angsty-books">emotional-angsty-books</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer517335605" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12931818675427628026"><b>
  <i>Will they or won't they?</i>
</b><br/><br/>That's <b>
  <u>all</u>
</b> this book is about. <br/><br/>If you haven't read this series yet, <b>
  <i>Stop!</i>
</b> Unless you're in the mood for reading about stuff that isn't going to make sense. This review is for the diehard fans...the ones that have struggled through all the Ivy nonsense and the Nick-Kisten-Marshal-Pierce drama. The ones that have cheered for Rachel from her early witch struggles to the maturity that she has shown in this book. <b>YOU</b> know who you are.<br/><br/>That's right...I'm talking to <i>y</i></span>
  <span id="freeText12931818675427628026" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Will they or won't they?</i>
</b><br><br>That's <b>
  <u>all</u>
</b> this book is about. <br><br>If you haven't read this series yet, <b>
  <i>Stop!</i>
</b> Unless you're in the mood for reading about stuff that isn't going to make sense. This review is for the diehard fans...the ones that have struggled through all the Ivy nonsense and the Nick-Kisten-Marshal-Pierce drama. The ones that have cheered for Rachel from her early witch struggles to the maturity that she has shown in this book. <b>YOU</b> know who you are.<br><br>That's right...I'm talking to <i>you</i>! And if you haven't read this book, what in the heck are you waiting for? Haven't we waited long enough? We've wanted Trent, well, we got him...bigger and better than ever! There is lots and <b>LOTS</b> of the cookie maker in this book and I have to say, it still wasn't enough! It's killing me knowing there's only one book left! ~Sob~ I think I might cry...but nope, I'll just deal with that later. {{{Can I get a group hug??}}}<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1393706657ra/8754909.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Back to the story...Strange magic waves are coming from Rach's ley line and causing charms to explode and basically cause chaos to ensue. On top of that, we learn that the master vampires are not waking up and something's going on with the living vampires. But what else is new? Same "everything is going to hell in a hand basket" that always happens in Rach's life...<i>and I loved every minute of it</i>. Okay, not <i>every</i> minute of it, but you get my drift.<br><br>And as if that's not enough to keep Rach busy, her and Trent go On. A. Date. That's right, folks...A DATE!! Can I get an AMEN?? And I have to tell you, the date was A-Ma-Zing! ~Sigh~ <br><br>But there's trouble in paradise and her name is Ellasbeth...that's right, The B*tch is back...Ugh! As if we couldn't hate her more. One thing I will give her credit for is that she seems to be doing an okay job as a Mom but....that's it! <br><br>KH had said that she is beginning to wrap things up and that is very clear in this book. There is <i>finally</i> some calmness with Ivy and Nina (hang on, you'll get there). David and the Weres seem to be coming together and again with Rach and her new maturity, she's able to see what needs to be done and does it! There's still chaos with the FIB and I.S...not really sure what's going to come out of that and with Edden but I'm hoping he's put in charge. <br><br>Of course, not everything has headed in that direction yet. A lot of things with characters are left up in the air. And there were some things that happened that I'm hoping will turn around. (Al...and his poor broken heart! I <i>finally</i> get him!) <br><br>And I can't forget the wonderful and hilarious Jenks! What would the series be without his particular brand of humor? I love all his one liners. But as much as I love him and Rachel together, I must admit, I really enjoy his relationship with Trent. <br><br>And then there's Bis...who would've thought a wayward baby gargoyle would touch your heart so much. I love how he is <i>always</i> there for Rach and he always helps her. I would even read a spin off series of him as an adult!<br><br>Okay, okay....More Trent you say?? Bwahahahaha...well, I'll never tell! Seriously, you just NEED to read it...it's sooo good. I will say the one thing that I absolutely LOVED <i>almost</i> more than <b>that one scene ;)</b> is how much Trent "gets" Rach. How he always knows what she's thinking and knows where she goes. Oh how it made my heart happy! ♥ Was that enough for you? ;)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1393706551i/8754906._SY540_.jpg" width="350" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(Witchy-poo and Cookie Maker)<br><br>I do have to say that there was some crazy stuff going on in this book...and it went wwwaaaayyy out there - a bit cray-cray if you know what I mean. But...I liked how it followed through and I liked how Newt factored in. *Fingers crossed* that the resolution will be just as good. <br><br>The ending...AMAZEBALLS! TOUCHE! AND GOOD RIDDANCE! BOOYA! Pheww...the whole book just wore me out. Thank you, <i>thank you</i>, <b>THANK YOU</b> Kim Harrison and just <u>please</u> continue on this same path for the last book...and don't switch things up!! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1381177006i/4453083.jpg" width="400" height="070" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>Favorite quotes</u>
</b> <br><i>(Proceed at your own risk! I tried to be good and I did refrain...begrudgingly!)</i><br><br>♥ “Yeah, the elf looks good in the sun,” Jenks smart-mouthed, the pixy currently sitting on the bottom of my hooped earrings and out of the moderate wind. “When you going to put us all out of your misery and boink him?”<br><br>♥ “They say you can tell a lot about a man by the ball he uses.”<br><br>♥ “Why does everyone assume I’m having sex with him?” I said, exasperated. <br><br>“Because he’s an elf, love, and elves are very good at it.”<br><br>♥ “Honestly, you’re both an embarrassment, rolling around in the dust, trying to see who has the biggest magic wand.”<br><br>♥ “I enjoyed last night,” he said softly, the words making me shiver, though it might be the sensation of his fingers hinting at pulling me back to him. “Riding,” he added, a gentle pressure building between us. “You before me. I’m glad you stayed on this time,” he added, smiling.<br><br>♥ “Rache . . .” Jenks rose up, his expression pleading as his dust hit the pan and sparkled. “I can’t believe I’m saying this, but you’re perfect for each other! You irritate people, and he smoothes things out. You have good mojo, and he only thinks he does. You’re broke, and he’s rich. You’ve got those weird feet of yours, and he’s got them cute ears.”<br><br>♥ "I did the right thing, what was acceptable and needed—and it worked. But it almost killed me.”<br><br>♥ “I like walking into a room and seeing your face light up when you see me.”<br><br>♥ “I want to wake up beside you, see your curls on my pillow. I want a chance at falling in love.”<br><br>♥ “Tell me you’ve not wanted to know for a long time,” he whispered, and I quailed as his hand touched my shoulder. “Tell me that, right now, and I will leave.”<br><br>♥ “I was kind of hoping you might not be a talker.” <br><br>I ran a foot up his pant leg, then back down. “Then give my lips something to do.”<br><br>♥ “I have a very sturdy house, Jenks,” Trent said. “So do you.”<br></span>

<div id="review_736019731" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/736019731" />
    <a title="Veronica " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7035111-veronica"><img alt="Veronica " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360466651p2/7035111.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/736019731?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Veronica " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Veronica " href="/user/show/7035111-veronica">Veronica </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7035111-veronica?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer736019731" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13537634064845545166">What can I say about a book that I’ve been waiting for since at least book three? To say that it was amazing, heartbreaking, uplifting, funny, life affirming, maddening, romantic, and bittersweet is all accurate and yet still woefully insufficient. The fact that this is the penultimate book in what will be a 13 book series makes it even that much more incredible. Most long running series outstay their “sell by” date and go out with a whimper, with some readers relieved, if not downright happy, t</span>
  <span id="freeText13537634064845545166" style="display:none">What can I say about a book that I’ve been waiting for since at least book three? To say that it was amazing, heartbreaking, uplifting, funny, life affirming, maddening, romantic, and bittersweet is all accurate and yet still woefully insufficient. The fact that this is the penultimate book in what will be a 13 book series makes it even that much more incredible. Most long running series outstay their “sell by” date and go out with a whimper, with some readers relieved, if not downright happy, to see them go. I predict that will not be the case with this series. I foresee, rather, that this series will do what all great series do…leave us wanting more. As for this particular installment, well…<br /><br />Rachel has had a rather quiet three months since the end of Ever After, the last book in the series. She’s filled her days by working as Trent’s security since Quen has been on the West Coast supervising Ellasbeth’s time with Ray and Lucy. That down time soon comes to a screeching halt, however, when spells start misfiring, causing all sorts of panic and chaos all over Cincinnati. As Rachel and the gang set about trying to figure out what’s causing magic to go wonky, they find a chain reaction of trouble ready to explode interspecies relations sky high. <br /><br />Along the way, we find out some really interesting things. While the demons and the Ever After don’t play as big a role here as they did in the last book, what IS there is important. Newt continues to be the crazy, wise woman who speaks in riddles. I still can’t decide if she was trying to warn Rachel off certain actions or if she was encouraging them. You never quite know what she’s going to say or do but that’s why I love her. Then there’s Al. Oh, Al. He made me feel sad for him; he made me feel annoyed with him. This is clearly a demon with some emotional baggage. We get a bit more of his backstory here, and it’s heartbreaking, but there is clearly still more to discover. Hopefully we’ll be getting it all in the next book because Al’s story clearly isn’t done.<br /><br />Ivy and Jenks are still in the mix and it was actually nice to see more of Ivy this time around than we’ve had of her lately. She continues to move forward with her life and it’s nice to see her so happy, even though she’s dealing with some stressful things in her own life. Jenks is ever his awesome self, providing the glue and the heart that holds everything together. I did miss Belle in this book since I find her relationship with Jenks cute. In addition to Rachel’s two BFFs, we also get the return of some key characters from past books playing integral roles in Rachel’s attempts to save the world…again. As this series is winding down, there is the definite sense that we are being given the chance to say goodbye, and to walk away knowing that these characters that we have grown to know and love will still be out there doing what they do best long after that last cover is closed. <br /><br />We also find out more about the current political climates for both the vampires and the elves and I expect that both will continue to play out in the final book. Up until now, we haven’t ever really had a good picture of elven society and how it works, outside of a few references made here and there throughout the series. We get quite a bit more information here as we meet two new elves and find out just how much Trent’s back is really up against the wall. To add insult to injury, Ellasbeth is back to help make sure that Trent tows the elven company line. God, but I really hate that woman. Just saying.<br /><br />Of course, this review wouldn’t be complete without talking about Trent. His parts with Rachel were some of my favorite from the book. Big surprise, I know. The three months that Rachel has spent working security for him have gone a long way towards shaping the nature of their relationship…and the questions of what is best, what is needed, and what is desired loom large. This was almost as much Trent’s book as it was Rachel’s, even though it’s all still told from her POV, so it’s fitting then that he shares the cover with her this time around. The fact that I could still feel Trent’s frustration and despair – and his hope – even through Rachel’s first person POV speaks volumes for Kim Harrison as a writer. Trent doesn’t have an easy road to travel in this installment (not that Ever After was any cakewalk) as he finds himself facing ultimatums from his species. Does he follow his head or his heart, and are they really two different things anymore? What do you do if the person you want to be, deep down to your soul, isn’t the person you’re expected to be? Trent has some hard decisions to make in this book, decisions with some huge costs and ramifications. I could say more…much, MUCH more…but all I will say is that there are some parts of this book that will be worthy of many, many re-reads.<br /><br />This book, as always, has some pretty great showdowns, fight sequences that get the job done but aren’t overly long (thank goodness!), chases – on horse even!, and daring rescues. I could talk about those but if you’re a Hollows fan you know that Rachel and her crew can kick some serious butt when they need to. So on that score, they deliver in spades in this book. What I really love though, what draws me in as a reader, what grabs hold of my heart and refuses to let go long after I’ve read the last word and closed the book are the characters and the way they relate to each other. So while this book has all the action you could want it’s also liberally sprinkled with those smaller, quieter character moments that infuse the story with heart and soul. Pure gold. And really, what more could you want?</span>
  <a data-text-id="13537634064845545166" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3772758816515053645"><b>2/7/18 - ON SALE for $1.99:</b><br/><br/><a href='https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B00DB3DBGI/ref=as_li_ss_il?ie=UTF8&linkCode=li1&tag=rabrea-20&linkId=b823c00a311b6187f668d98fa1d25ac7' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>

</a><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517569706i/24988333.gif' width='1' height='1' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://amzn.to/2nIbFX2'>http://amzn.to/2nIbFX2</a><br/><br/><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2014/03/review-the-undead-pool-by-kim-harrison.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/>So I realize that I’m diving straight into this without having reviewed the previous ELEVEN (it makes me happy that “eleven” is so close to “elves”) books, but I promise I’ll get to them before the series ends next year.<br/><br/>*sobs*<br/><br/>I’m also going to do my darnedest to not be spoilery for this particular book, but as it’s the <i>twelfth</i> book, avoiding spoilers for the series in its entirety is probably beyond my abilitie</span>
  <span id="freeText3772758816515053645" style="display:none"><b>2/7/18 - ON SALE for $1.99:</b><br><br><a href="https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B00DB3DBGI/ref=as_li_ss_il?ie=UTF8&amp;linkCode=li1&amp;tag=rabrea-20&amp;linkId=b823c00a311b6187f668d98fa1d25ac7" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1424110110i/13717378.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517569706i/24988333.gif" width="1" height="1" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://amzn.to/2nIbFX2">http://amzn.to/2nIbFX2</a><br><br><b>3.5 stars</b><br><br><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2014/03/review-the-undead-pool-by-kim-harrison.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br>So I realize that I’m diving straight into this without having reviewed the previous ELEVEN (it makes me happy that “eleven” is so close to “elves”) books, but I promise I’ll get to them before the series ends next year.<br><br>*sobs*<br><br>I’m also going to do my darnedest to not be spoilery for this particular book, but as it’s the <i>twelfth</i> book, avoiding spoilers for the series in its entirety is probably beyond my abilities. You have been dully warned.<br><br>Kim Harrison’s <i>The Hollows</i> is my second favorite Urban Fantasy series, and as such, it’s one of the series that I’ve bothered my friends and family into reading. I love it. They love it. Everyone is happy. Especially now that it seems like Trent and Rachel are finally getting their shit together.<br><br>Since the very beginning, I’ve had a thing for Trent. Rachel’s had half a dozen flings along the way (that have all ended in varying degrees of BAD), but Trent . . . of all the jerk-of-my-dreams characters in the world, he may be my favorite.<br><br>*sighs wistfully*<br><br>SO everyone who shared this perspective was THRILLED a few books back when his and Rachel’s relationship began to change. Ever since then, Harrison has seemed to be leading us towards a happily ever after (HA), but did it finally happen in <i>The Undead Pool</i>?! I’ll never tell.<br><br>READ IT. *smirks*<br><br>In <i>The Undead Pool</i>, Rachel has been providing security for Trent for the past three months while Quen is in Cali with Ellasbeth and the girls (who are due to arrive back any day now). The sexual tension will blow. Your. Friggin’. Mind. The last night before Rachel is off the job, Cincy goes to Hell—something is causing magical misfires of epic proportions.<br><br>At this point I feel it’s necessary to inform you that I’ve been in a bit of a book funk. I don’t seem to be loving much of anything right now, so there’s a distinct possibility that when the re-read occurs next year, I’ll be all “OMG that book was AMAZING.” Right now, however, something just didn’t quite jive for me. Can you guess what it was?<br><br>The freaking mystics.<br><br>I mean what in the world? An Elvish goddess who’s not really a goddess, but a collective mind made up of energy whose individual thoughts (&lt;—–the mystics) are sentient, but who <i>may</i> have been an actual goddess (tangible person) once upon a time?<br><br>Huh?<br><br>AND Rachel has been concerned over the state of Ivy’s soul (or the lack of one when she transitions from living vampire to undead) almost since the beginning, and for probably the last half of the series, she’s been actively trying to come up with a solution. I think that that’s the endgame for <i>The Hollows</i>—finding a way for vampires to keep their souls.<br>The point is that we’ve all known for a while what was coming.<br><br>BUT this lead-in just felt . . . I don’t know, contrived? A previously unheard of sect of vampires out to take over (at the very least) the vampire portion of the supernatural races? We’d never heard of the Humans-Against-Whatever from <i>A Perfect Blood</i> either, but at least when the concept was introduced there were background stories to support its existence. This time it was just BOOM: Free Vampires.<br><br>And the whole situation was engineered by what/who?<br><br>David at some point in this book says that Rachel saved Trent—that Trent had been headed down a completely different and <i>ruthless</i> path, but Rachel saved him from himself. Maybe Harrison was drawing a parallel about the kind of man Trent would have become without Rachel’s influence. Maybe. Probably. Whatever.<br><br>Intentional parallel or not, all the ends and outs of this installment didn’t gel for me the way others have. It was still good. I love Rachel and Trent and Jenks and everyone else, and Harrison upheld all of the established elements of her series—there is nothing out of left field here (unlike a not-to-be-named other series that ended recently). But all the time I spent with my brow furrowed in confusion while I was reading makes this a four star book for me. I wasn’t able to just sink into the story and let it take me over.<br><br>Still, <i>The Hollows</i> continues to have a cast of characters that is both original and dynamic, and its conclusion next year is sure to be bittersweet. Don’t let the series’ end catch you unawares—get caught up and soon!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>My other reviews for this series:</b><br><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351599255" rel="nofollow noopener">Dead Witch Walking (The Hollows #1)</a>

<div id="review_847851998" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/847851998" />
    <a title="Pia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21498870-pia"><img alt="Pia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372002772p2/21498870.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/847851998?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pia" href="/user/show/21498870-pia">Pia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18098816-the-undead-pool">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer847851998" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2965852599275540858"><b>Who are you and what have you done to Rachel ?!</b><br/><br/>I finally finished reading TUP this morning and I've been struggling to decide how many stars to give it ever since, vacillating between 2 and 4. So I've been doing what I do best, procrastinating in putting in my rating and review and finally decided on 3 stars, for now.<br/><br/>To say that I had been looking forward to this book is a huge understatement. <br/>I had it all planned out, reading the first 5 chapters on the 24th, getting up at 6 am on the 25th (rel</span>
  <span id="freeText2965852599275540858" style="display:none"><b>Who are you and what have you done to Rachel ?!</b><br /><br />I finally finished reading TUP this morning and I've been struggling to decide how many stars to give it ever since, vacillating between 2 and 4. So I've been doing what I do best, procrastinating in putting in my rating and review and finally decided on 3 stars, for now.<br /><br />To say that I had been looking forward to this book is a huge understatement. <br />I had it all planned out, reading the first 5 chapters on the 24th, getting up at 6 am on the 25th (release time where I live) so I could read a few chapters before having to leave for work and taking a day off from work on the 26th to finish reading and digest. So it's not as if I didn't want to love this book, because I really, really did, which might explain my huge disappointment.<br /><br />And truth be told, I really enjoyed the first 9 chapters, as well as the final 2 (and even the 22th, even though I don't ship Trent, it was well written). My favorite, however must be the 9th chapter, that was chuck full of information that I believe will be important in the grand scheme of things, and I look forward to all the speculation and discussion it will doubt entice over the coming year. But most of the rest was just meh, boring, and dragged on endlessly.<br /><br />Besides that, I have some other huge issues with this book and my rating may well drop further if the 'Trend(t)' started here is continued in the final book of the series. <br />On the other hand, on the slim chance that the 'out of character Rachel' in TUP is a plot device to set up a turnaround in the final installment, I'll bump this up to 4 stars (one can hope, and I'm trying to cheer myself up here).<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />This book irritated my inner feminist no end and I'll be seriously pissed if Rachel ends up barefoot, pregnant, enslaved and domesticated by the end of the series (which strangely enough, a lot of female readers are rooting for, and believe will happen – oh well, kudos to them, but I don't get it). <br /><br />For one thing, Rachel seemed completely out of character in this book, so much so that it got on my nerves after a while.<br /><br />Gone is independent runner, kick-ass Rachel. <br />Gone the adrenaline junkie who enjoyed riding up front on Ivy's bike as a mink.<br /><br />Instead we get an elf-struck shadow of her former self, doing things she wouldn't have dreamed of in book 1 and thinking things such as <br /><i>“I would have gotten mad, but Trent was staring at my mouth. If the table wasn't between us, I think he would have kissed me. The thought was almost as good as actually doing is, and my bad mood vanished”</i><br />Yep, Elf-struck it is.<br /><br />I could still overlook her acting as a caddie during chapter 1, although KH should've checked the rules of golf before coming up with the ridiculous notion that someone teeing off on a par 3 with people putting still on the green, would get away with it (basic golf etiquette, but I digress). But still, caddie ? Really ? WTH?<br />Later on in the book, it seemed that she had traded in her brains and brawls for drooling over Trent and the kiddies, so much so that it got boring (how many times can you read how tight his ass is or how well he smells before becoming suspicious that he put some whammy on her).<br />And then, from chapter 19 on IIRC, she's totally erratic and confused, due to the mystic-stuff, which made the first POV fairly pointless and boring (btw, where did fun drunk Rachel go, the one yelling out of a car whilst out of it ? – the mystic confused one was no fun at all).<br /><br />The sex scene was pretty hot, but I can't help but wonder about Al's warning :<br /><i>“He's going to seduce her and enslave her, and us with her!”</i><br />as can only hope that Newt's advice has some prophesy to it :<br /><i>“Go collect your elf from Gally before the silly demon kills him. You're going to want the pleasure of that yourself”</i><br /><br />And I hated to see her scared and playing second fiddle to Trent on the train. The old Rachel would've thrived at the chance to have Etude drop her on the train, and she wouldn't have played backup to anyone (Jenks is still backup to Rachel, Trent didn't replace him there – no, as I see it, our former runner is playing backup to Trent now, just where he wanted her in the first place). Dang, I miss the Rachel who loved to go out on a run.<br /><br />Btw, anyone else remember this for DWW ?<br /><i>“I'm going to break you, Morgan, until you will do anything to get out of that cage. I do hope it takes a while. Jon took nearly fifteen years. Not as a rat, but a slave all the same. I imagine you will break a lot faster.”</i><br />and<br /><i>“Even so, he never knew I was breaking him. Most don't. He still doesn't. And if you suggested it, he would kill you.”</i><br /><br />Yep, enslavement seems to be the name of the game, and seeing as Trent had no qualms letting Quen put the slave ring on Rachel only recently, it doesn't seem that the leopard has change his spots.<br /><br />So when I read Rachel thinking <br /><i>“I didn't mind being a part of his publicity program, and the man did need protection”</i><br />I couldn't help but feel sad at the fact that he has, in fact broken her, and she doesn't even realize it. So not what I'm looking for in an UF featuring a kick-ass heroine.<br /><br />I can totally understand why Al was so upset with her (at one point, I felt like putting her out of her missery myself, but I haven't given up hope yet – poor Al).<br /><br />Speaking of a leopard not changing its spots, Trent was actually in character for the good first part of the book, being the same old male chauvinist prick, that is. <br />He was as slick and manipulative as ever, doing whatever he wants without a care in the world about hurting her (throwing her into her circle in the EA, brushing her off on the phone, not telling her what she needs to know and taking away her choices). <br /><br />Frankly, I don't understand what anyone sees in him. He's nothing but an arrogant, lying, cheating jerk, even now keeping secrets from her, which she called him out on several times ('not' being able to pass the road blocks, giving Newt riding lessons,...).<br />And Rachel is delusional if she believes he won't cheat on her. But then, women are always blind-sighting themselves in that department, wanting to believe they're special and surely, he didn't love the former misses as much as he loves her,... yeah, good luck with that (he had no qualms cheating on Ellasbeth is all I'm saying).<br /><br />So, anyhow, big surprise when the same Trent, who killed his lab chief and the were who wanted to join David's pack, as well as I who knows how many other people, suddenly begins acting like mother Theresa, saying things like <br /><i>“If we can't stop a train without killing innocents, then we don't deserve the freedom we have”</i><br />Yikes. Gag. I really could've done without reading that. Hypocrite much.<br /><br />Sorry, but I don't trust him any further than I can throw him, which is, not at all. IMO he's pulling the wool over Rachel's eyes, lying and cheating as ever, and with a big ace up his sleeve.<br />In fact, I don't buy it that he's destitute. A big planner, hot shot millionaire must've heard of off shore banking and I can't imagine someone like Trent not planning for the eventuality he's outed (otherwise, it's bad writing, and I refuse to believe that at this point). As he said himself “he has insurance”.<br /><br />I don't believe he's sacrificing everything he has in order to be with Rachel either. IMO he's just upping the stakes, swapping he's chances of elven domination by marrying Ellasbeth, to chances of world domination over all species by attaching himself to the only day walking demon Rachel.<br /><br />Remember this ?<br /><i>“An elf who doesn't believe in his magic can be bested. One who believes will always survive”</i><br />and<br /><i>“Birthright is given. Power is earned. I still have it, and it is growing, not failing. … You haven't seen de depths of what I'm capable of.”</i><br /><br />So I'm kinda hoping the man has an ace up his sleeve, and Rachel will realize it and snap out of her subservient role and kick his ass.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />If not, TUP is just another weak PNR, and I've been waisting my time, again.<br />The undead storyline and the goddess-confusion certainly didn't get my juices flowing and the book lacked the light hearted humor of the others in the series (so I missed that as well), so in the end, it took me forever to get through.<br /><br />So fingers crossed for next year.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2965852599275540858" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_540545665" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/540545665" />
    <a title="Carol (StarAngel&#39;s Reviews) Allen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6294320-carol-starangel-s-reviews-allen"><img alt="Carol (StarAngel&#39;s Reviews) Allen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386893634p2/6294320.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/540545665?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol (StarAngel&#39;s Reviews) Allen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol (StarAngel&#39;s Reviews) Allen" href="/user/show/6294320-carol-starangel-s-reviews-allen">Carol (StarAngel&#39;s Reviews) Allen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6294320-carol-starangel-s-reviews-allen?shelf=all-time-favorite">all-time-favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6294320-carol-starangel-s-reviews-allen?shelf=5-star-books">5-star-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6294320-carol-starangel-s-reviews-allen?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer540545665" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8181050321257980896"><strong>Book</strong> – The Undead Pool (The Hollows #12)<br/><strong>Author</strong> – Kim Harrison<br/><strong>Publication Date</strong> – February 25, 2014<br/><strong>Type</strong> – Part of Series<br/><strong>Genre</strong> – Paranormal Romance<br/><strong>Rating</strong> – 6 out of 5 Stars<br/><br/><strong>Review</strong><br/>Ok….please bear with me – this is the first Paranormal book I have the pleasure of reviewing.  Yeah – I have read hundreds of them when I was addicted to this genre…..but for some reason – I can’t help but love and continue to read The Hollows series.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1393812555i/8767455._SY540_.jpg' alt='' width='540' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>It’s kind of funny but years ago when I first picked up Book #1 – I read t</span>
  <span id="freeText8181050321257980896" style="display:none"><strong>Book</strong> – The Undead Pool (The Hollows #12)<br><strong>Author</strong> – Kim Harrison<br><strong>Publication Date</strong> – February 25, 2014<br><strong>Type</strong> – Part of Series<br><strong>Genre</strong> – Paranormal Romance<br><strong>Rating</strong> – 6 out of 5 Stars<br><br><strong>Review</strong><br>Ok….please bear with me – this is the first Paranormal book I have the pleasure of reviewing.  Yeah – I have read hundreds of them when I was addicted to this genre…..but for some reason – I can’t help but love and continue to read The Hollows series.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1393812555i/8767455._SY540_.jpg" alt="" width="540" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It’s kind of funny but years ago when I first picked up Book #1 – I read the first few pages and put it back down – I was bored to tears ---- a few months later I saw it sitting on my Nook and decided to try again and once I got past the first few chapters….I was fucking HOOKED!!  This is the only series that continues to have me going back for more and more of Rachel, Ivy, Jenks, Trent ---- my GOD….it’s like they are my freakin’ family!<br><br>I waited and waited for this book – I requested it on Edelweiss and got turned down (poopy heads) so I had to wait for the release day.  My God….this book – I can’t even begin to explain the emotions I went through in reading it.  I was pissed…..so fucking pissed at the circumstances surrounding Rachel and Trent.  For so many years, I have waited for these two to FINALLY realize that they make a great team.  And for me hating Trent so much in the earlier episodes, he really did a 360 in his attitude and his actions.  Hahahahaaa….I still remember when he held Rachel captive in a little cage acting like she was his pet!! What a dickhead he was back then.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1393812555i/8767456._SY540_.jpg" alt="" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You know I thought after Kirsten – that Rachel would never be happy again – they were perfect together….hahahaha….well the best a vampire and demon could be…right?<br><br>But put together an elf and a demon….whoah….now that’s something to write home about!!<br><br>Ms. Harrison does it every time….she captivates me and takes me on an adventure through the Hollows, through the ley lines, through the ever after and through Cincy. For a book being over 500 pages – I was upset when I got to the end….I wanted more. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1393812555i/8767457._SY540_.jpg" alt="" width="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Like what is going to happen with Rachel and Trent?  What about Al? (Yeah he really pissed me off) I don’t think Ellsabeth is done wrecking havoc….have we seen the last of her?  I want more Newt….<br><br>Please tell me Ms. Harrison that this isn’t the last we will be reading about my favorite demon, vampire, pixie, elf and werewolf!!<br><br><strong>Re-Cap</strong><br>Rachel is at it again….a walking time bomb clutz – this time magic is misfiring and it seems to be coming from her ley line.  The undead vampire masters have fallen into a deep sleep and can’t be woken while the “free vampires” are making life in Cincy dangerous.  With the help of all Rachel’s friends they figure out who is behind the mess but why is Newt catching fireflies and calling it magic?  What could this possibly have to do with the troubles in Cincy?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1393812555i/8767458.jpg" alt="" width="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Through all of this, Trent is acting different – he is taking risks and enjoying the hell out of himself.  With Qwen gone and Rachel as his security, he is riding the high life of being “normal” Well that is until Ellsabeth shows up along with the Elven priests and pressures Trent into finalizing his engagement to Ellsabeth.  It’s the right thing to do in order to keep the West and East Coast elves unified.<br><br>But then why is Trent taking Rachel out on a close to “normal” date by going bowling and eating greasy food?  Is there more to this?<br><br><strong>Wrap-Up</strong><br>Ms. Harrison NEVER disappoints with her Hollows series!  And the more she writes – the more I want to read!<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="8181050321257980896" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Montzalee Wittmann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Montzalee Wittmann" href="/user/show/32532051-montzalee-wittmann">Montzalee Wittmann</a>
