        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1985474806" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6209367744422009511"> The Undead Pool (The Hollows #12) by Kim Harrison continues with another winning book in the Hollows series. I love the interaction between vamps, elves, demons, were, humans, and more. In this book, many things are going on but the many thing is a magic attack in not only attacking the city but tracking Rachel. Something is putting the master vampires to sleep...Rachel is feeling more for Trenton....ah...I love these books!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_646053427" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/646053427" />
    <a title="Shayla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10794394-shayla"><img alt="Shayla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1397695707p2/10794394.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/646053427?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

The Undead Pool was a great book, however i am not looking forward to the next one as it symbolizes the end of a series that i live and have come to dream about. </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_621762480" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/621762480" />
    <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder"><img alt="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572373103p2/3048260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/621762480?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder">Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=a-own-book-form">a-own-book-form</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=witches">witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=didnt-like-ending">didnt-like-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=magic-powers">magic-powers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=demons">demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=part-of-series">part-of-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer621762480" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8671476720726564258"><br/><br/><b>Warning – there are spoilers in this review. </b><br/><br/>The Hollows series has remained my favorite series for several years– it has everything I want in a continued world – darkness, humor, the supernatural done right, exciting plotlines that are focused on, amazing characterization, and addicting dialogue. Pretty much all my fangirl buttons are pushed. To say I was excited to read this book is an understatement. Just like last year, I made sure I had the day off from work to sit all day and read this the</span>
  <span id="freeText8671476720726564258" style="display:none"><br /><br /><b>Warning – there are spoilers in this review. </b><br /><br />The Hollows series has remained my favorite series for several years– it has everything I want in a continued world – darkness, humor, the supernatural done right, exciting plotlines that are focused on, amazing characterization, and addicting dialogue. Pretty much all my fangirl buttons are pushed. To say I was excited to read this book is an understatement. Just like last year, I made sure I had the day off from work to sit all day and read this the day of its release. Like last year, I ordered some sort of special food I’d been craving and hardly get to eat. I do nothing else but read and relax during a Hollows reading day, treating myself to the newest release of my favorite series.<br /><br />The book is about 430 pages, and in its paper walls there is a lot of action (at first, and at the ending). The first part of the book is especially charming, opening up with a golf scene and the inevitable dating that comes with Trent and Rachel. The bowling scene was sweet, awesome, and a perfect first date. The fight scene which followed rocked with Rachel showing how many tricks she has developed up her sleeve under Al’s direction and her own study.<br /><br />I dug how much Jenks was in the book, flittering around from scene to scene as a friend, partner, and relationship encourager. He teased with his typical raunchiness, provided some of the best lines of the story as usual - where would we be without Jenks? I was a bit bothered by a line he says to Rachel at the end about picking her new partner to watch her back, but I like to think he’s not being replaced, but sees changes coming. So many of his kids have grown and left, so there is a change of emptiness while reading those scenes. There’s still plenty of them flying around to provide pixie fun.<br /><br />The main storyline with the goddess and mystics was intriguing and creatively done. I applaud Kim for her originality and how complexly layered the details. The scene with the 'summoning' and the bodies was simply creepy *shiver*. I do hope the goddess plot is done with and that the next book focuses on resolving its roots, but it was cool to have it in this one. I personally never had an issue with Rachel being a pure demon and a powerful one at that, so I do hope it’s not mellowed further by having to add more of the elven stuff into her. I always liked our itchy witch fine the way she was the other books – demon, witchy, independent.<br /><br />David has been seen little in several books but makes a comeback here often. He has always been an enchanting character. We get to see Eden again, which is awesome. I always loved his father-figure, protective character. <br /><br />Rachel finally says goodbye to a role that I feel she should say goodbye to. Letting go here makes sense and is how I figured it would happen. <br /><br />Ivy is a focus in the story. In some of the previous books she has been around a little less, but here she’s present in the first half quite a bit. She also seems calmer and to be changing because of her relationship with Nina. There are still signs of the tough vampire we all know and love, but overall she has really started mellowing out. A change that’s been obviously coming is spelled out in this book. I did have an issue with how often Rachel kept mentally repeating why they can’t work and would work better apart, because really this isn’t true. They wouldn't work as a romantic relationship, but I always thought they always worked so well together as friends and partners. I’d like to think they always stay close and active in each other’s lives, helping each other when it’s needed. I don’t see why it keeps getting so clearly pointed out about them not working out romantically when that was resolved so many books ago.<br /><br />The Undead Pool as its title and the beginning focusing on vampires made me think this installment would focus more on the fanged fiends and lead the way towards resolving a main plot element (Ivy) present from book one. Instead the vampires are there in mention sometimes, but it mainly focuses on the elves and their goddess. Eventually the vampire angle basically disappears besides brief mention to be overshadowed by all things elvish.<br /><br />This is where I started to get bugged. It’s making it clear again that all things Elf are superior (I disagree, but the series has somehow become elf obsessed because of Trent) – their magic is now superior, they are superior, their cultures (never saw that from the other books, but since Trent is making the spotlight, it’s being focused on now.) For a book of this length, so much time is spent on the angst and buildup in Rachel’s head of her and Trent’s relationship. <br /><br />For once the plot of the Hollows takes too much of a backseat to just have relationship speak. It becomes more of a paranormal romance when it’s always been a straight Urban Fantasy series. She repeatedly – and I mean, repeatedly – keeps mentioning the lines of Trent’s backside and body as he walks by. His smell is in every scene he’s in, mentioned often. And now that he is here, it seems almost everyone else is taking a backseat – either pushed out of the way entirely or replaced. I know things change, that’s to be expected, but I see no reason why her other relationships can’t still exist and keep evolving too. Just getting a man in her life should not replace all that and strip Rachel down to such a simplistic character.<br /><br />Al, my favorite, is in a few scenes at the beginning, but never to be seen again until the end, where a heartbreaking scene makes it way for about two pages. I really hope this is resolved in the next book, and resolved well, otherwise I will feel haunted. To me one of the main aspects of the series has been Rachel finding out what she is and exploring that side, and evolving into the teacher/student/friend bond with Al. Through that she learns more about the demons. <br /><br />His reaction at the end was harsh and I disliked the end wrap-up. I felt hollow afterwards and cheated. His reaction was based on fear, protection of self, and betrayal. I would have liked a different ending for the book but we shall wait and see for the next book what is resolved. I also thought the scene with another character at the very end was a bit silly.<br /><br />I disliked the backset and again feel that since Trent is here, almost everyone else is seeming less important. I see no reason why that would happen. Rachel never fit that stereotype. She always had such an interesting, layered life. Seeing her bared down to Trent’s side raising his children and riding horses in fields never fit into the picture as all she is and all she can be. Cool if she does that too, but I like the excitement before that she kept around, other people she would relate to, outside interests that were her own. She was always independent. <br /><br />At least we know what happens with Nick. <br /><br />Newt was epic in this book. Her tea party scene was priceless and she gives good advice on the Trent situation. Her ending scene was focused on the elves a bit more as well, but she was severely needed in the book. Her advice was sage. I do keep wondering, with how wise she has always been and how true her words turn out, if her words during the tea scene about Rachel wanting to do something (avoiding spoilers) herself will come true in the future. I can’t see how the betrayal would happen as it doesn’t fit into character we know, but with all the foreshadowing perhaps one day it will. I really doubt Kim Harrison will end the series with a betrayal as she is just building up a relationship and has to tie the races together, so there wouldn’t be plausibility or time to have that happen. I guess it is something the reader is supposed to wonder about happening off-page in the future. <br /><br />With only one book left, I worry about so much still needing wrapped up and solved. We have a major story with Ivy left to get fixed, the demon/elf thing, fixing of a relationship (I pray anyway!). These are all big things, but with Kim being such a talented author who has created such a brilliant series, I’m sure the last book will do everything well.<br /><br />Overall there were issues I had with the book, but being a Hollows book of course I loved it too. I worry about some of the regulars seeming a little sanitized this time around and bothered by such a surprising series relying on a few predictable developments. I think a little magic has been dampered as a few relationships, especially the new ones, seem forced and a bit dull. Despite these issues it was another excellent story with a creative development, a major fighting battle where everyone shone in their roles, some wonderful scenes I will re-read often, and is an enjoyable book that is well on its way to wrapping up an epic world that will cause misery to me when it ends.<br /><br />At least the Hollows can always be kept alive in the minds of fans and by re-reads. But still, thank God for another book next year :)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8671476720726564258" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_863483080" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/863483080" />
    <a title="Jen Davis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4669344-jen-davis"><img alt="Jen Davis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548427639p2/4669344.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/863483080?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen Davis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen Davis" href="/user/show/4669344-jen-davis">Jen Davis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer863483080" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12130980283614503921">With the notable exception of A Perfect Blood, the Hollows has been steadily gaining momentum in the past few years. Each book is better than the one before. Each book has reminded me why I love this series so damn much. And once again, with this new installment, I have a new favorite. And frankly, I don't know how Kim Harrison is going to top this one. In fact, part of me wants to just stop reading right here, so she can't sucker-punch me at the end of the series.<br/><br/>I'm going to do my very best no</span>
  <span id="freeText12130980283614503921" style="display:none">With the notable exception of A Perfect Blood, the Hollows has been steadily gaining momentum in the past few years. Each book is better than the one before. Each book has reminded me why I love this series so damn much. And once again, with this new installment, I have a new favorite. And frankly, I don't know how Kim Harrison is going to top this one. In fact, part of me wants to just stop reading right here, so she can't sucker-punch me at the end of the series.<br /><br />I'm going to do my very best not to spoil you, since the surprising path of the journey is part of the joy. But I will confirm things you already know if you've looked at the cover or read the blurb. You'll note that for the first time, Rachel is not alone on the cover. Trent is right there with her. He is her co-star both in the cover-art and on the page. This isn't just Rachel's book. It's Rachel and Trent's book.<br /><br />Does that mean they finally get together? (*shifty eyes*) Of course, I can't answer that.<br /><br />One of the things I loved so much about this book is that you can really see how much Rachel has grown. She still has fears, both about her choices in life and her choices in men. But the biggest difference we are seeing in her, is that she no longer hides from those fears, she meets them head on. Her hiding and avoidance of her issues was one of the biggest disappointments in A Perfect Blood --and why it was a bit of a letdown for me. This is, well, not a new Rachel, but an improved one. She asks herself the tough questions and she thinks before she makes her choices.<br /><br />Not once did I get frustrated with the progression of the story. Not once did I want to smack Rachel. Or Ivy, even. I enjoyed watching these characters I have fallen in love with, evolve. It almost felt like a flashforward. I can see where everyone is going with their lives. Ivy. Jenks. David. The pack. The elves. Ellasbeth. Trent. Almost all of our secondary characters are back or at least get a mention for perspective. And you can really feel that their stories are finding resolution.<br /><br />I ran the gamut of emotions... fear, excitement, melancholy, elation. The plot moves quickly and takes a surprising path. Of course, there is a huge problem that only Rachel can solve. She faces grave danger as she fights to save the day and she relies on the resourcefulness of her family of friends to help her succeed. All this, while facing the derision of others. It's a formula that works for these books, and Harrison does a great job mixing up the particulars to keep it fresh.<br /><br />Will everyone love this book as much as I did? Maybe not. I think that for UF purists, it might have too much of the relationship/ romantic elements. But to all the shippers out there, it will be like a sparkly gift from heaven.<br /><br />To me, this could have served as a series finale. I could walk away happy. Which scares me to death. Because Kim Harrison is a sadistic killer. She can't let me stay happy... can she? What will she throw at us before Rachel's story is over? Somebody hold me.<br /><br />Rating: A<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12130980283614503921" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6449935572204499692">I feel like this should be one of my favorites of the series because...you know, Trent! And while I did love that he got such a starring role, the rest of it seemed oddly scattered. At the end, I wasn't sure what the point of the book was. What happened here that moved the series forward? A couple of major character relationships (both good and bad) moved forward, but other than that, I felt like it was a bit of a letdown. <br/><br/>I do find it cool that the demon world and the elven world are really col</span>
  <span id="freeText6449935572204499692" style="display:none">I feel like this should be one of my favorites of the series because...you know, Trent! And while I did love that he got such a starring role, the rest of it seemed oddly scattered. At the end, I wasn't sure what the point of the book was. What happened here that moved the series forward? A couple of major character relationships (both good and bad) moved forward, but other than that, I felt like it was a bit of a letdown. <br /><br />I do find it cool that the demon world and the elven world are really colliding. I suppose that this was kind of a transition, or preparation for the final book. So in that respect, it was great. </span>

<div id="review_683669142" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/683669142" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8711587-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484863713p2/8711587.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/683669142?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/8711587-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18098816-the-undead-pool">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8711587-angela?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer683669142" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10710015736908823502">So the book is probably a 3.5 and while I liked parts of it there were parts I felt didn't quite gel with me. I loved every scene Newt was in and she pretty much stole the show whenever she was on page. There wasn't enough Al, for me and being the Al lover I am, I had hoped he would have a greater role given events in the previous outing Ever After. But there wasn't a lot of the demons in here and there wasn't a lot of demon magic at all.<br/><br/>This book was more centred around the elves and their wild</span>
  <span id="freeText10710015736908823502" style="display:none">So the book is probably a 3.5 and while I liked parts of it there were parts I felt didn't quite gel with me. I loved every scene Newt was in and she pretty much stole the show whenever she was on page. There wasn't enough Al, for me and being the Al lover I am, I had hoped he would have a greater role given events in the previous outing Ever After. But there wasn't a lot of the demons in here and there wasn't a lot of demon magic at all.<br /><br />This book was more centred around the elves and their wild magic, which was just okay for me. I didn't enjoy the Goddess and mystics storylines as I have with other stories which featured the Weres or Ku'Sox. I've also been ready for the vampire story arc to be over for some time as well.<br /><br />Trent and Rachel shippers will be happy as at least that angle seems to have been resolved. We have seen Rachel grow over the series, so I think in my head I was ready for some real demon badass action and not the wild magic direction this story took. Rachel has learnt to use her friends to help her and not just work solo with only Jenks as back up, but this story took this to the other extreme, with every man and his dog helping her. <br /><br />So, what did I enjoy besides Newt? I loved Bis and his mean as computer skills, I loved Jenks one liners. I also enjoyed seeing Edden back again.<br /><br />Where was Belle? Barely mentioned and the characters did spend some time in the church? I'm still on board with the series, as I know the demons have to be front and centre in the final book. Not too fussed on the elves though. Even if the elves and demons appear to be forever linked.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10710015736908823502" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer559911077" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15440810400741336286">Welcome back to the Hollows! In the twelfth book of the series, Kim Harrison gives readers exactly what they have been wishing for in THE UNDEAD POOL.<br/><br/>Witch and day-walking demon, Rachel Morgan has yet another problem that has been wreaking havoc on Cincinnati. Spells have been misfiring all over the place, but seem to be originating her from ley line. This puts her in a spot responsible for cleaning up this mess, but when the union between humans and the Inderlanders rock on shaky ground, she is</span>
  <span id="freeText15440810400741336286" style="display:none">Welcome back to the Hollows! In the twelfth book of the series, Kim Harrison gives readers exactly what they have been wishing for in THE UNDEAD POOL.<br /><br />Witch and day-walking demon, Rachel Morgan has yet another problem that has been wreaking havoc on Cincinnati. Spells have been misfiring all over the place, but seem to be originating her from ley line. This puts her in a spot responsible for cleaning up this mess, but when the union between humans and the Inderlanders rock on shaky ground, she is wondering if maybe this is a task too big even for her. With undead master vampires also posing an issue, it could be an all-out war if this mess isn't contained immediately.<br /><br />Meanwhile, Harrison toys the with concept of romance between Rachel and Trent, her love interest for what seems like too long now. As they toe around each other, giving hints and sharing kisses, readers are kept on the precipice as Harrison addresses the question of Will they ever get together?<br /><br />With Harrison's stellar writing and amazing worldbuilding, it's really no wonder why this series has gained such a following. The characters continue to grow, the world is constantly changing and each plot in the books feel fresh and new. There is no question that THE UNDEAD POOL is the best of the series!<br /><br /><b>Reviewed for <a href="http://freshfiction.com/review.php?id=41231" rel="nofollow noopener"> Fresh Fiction</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="15440810400741336286" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_826930982" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/826930982" />
    <a title="JB" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6252434-jb"><img alt="JB" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593031648p2/6252434.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/826930982?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="JB" class="user" itemprop="url" name="JB" href="/user/show/6252434-jb">JB</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6252434-jb?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6252434-jb?shelf=witches-wizards-magic">witches-wizards-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6252434-jb?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6252434-jb?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6252434-jb?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6252434-jb?shelf=demons">demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6252434-jb?shelf=received-for-review">received-for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6252434-jb?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6252434-jb?shelf=book-in-a-series">book-in-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6252434-jb?shelf=sexual-tension">sexual-tension</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer826930982" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9230355293829136588"><i>**Find this and other reviews at <a href='http://www.thedemonlibrarian.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Demon Librarian</a>**</i><br/><br/><b>
  <i>So Worth The Wait!</i>
</b><br/><br/>I can't talk about the Hollows series without devolving into a gushing, nonsensical, fangirly mess. It's simply not possible. Kim Harrison has wowed and amazed me so many times, over so many years, that at this point if you were to tell me she walks on water, leaps tall buildings in a single bound, or has discovered the cure for cancer, my response would be, "Well duh, of course she has! It's KIM!" <br/><br/>The Undead Pool, thoug</span>
  <span id="freeText9230355293829136588" style="display:none"><i>**Find this and other reviews at <a href="http://www.thedemonlibrarian.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Demon Librarian</a>**</i><br /><br /><b>
  <i>So Worth The Wait!</i>
</b><br /><br />I can't talk about the Hollows series without devolving into a gushing, nonsensical, fangirly mess. It's simply not possible. Kim Harrison has wowed and amazed me so many times, over so many years, that at this point if you were to tell me she walks on water, leaps tall buildings in a single bound, or has discovered the cure for cancer, my response would be, "Well duh, of course she has! It's KIM!" <br /><br />The Undead Pool, though....this is THE BOOK, the one fans of the series have been dying to read for what feels like forever. Those of you not familiar with the series can't understand what we Hollows diehards have suffered. We've been brilliantly and ruthlessly teased, tormented, and outright tortured for so many books now that just thinking about it turns us into blubbering messes. We stammer, forget all the big words we know, and gesture wildly, like the mad people we are. And what's more, not only do we fully embrace the crazy, we feel sorry for all of you who haven't experienced it!<br /><br />But what, exactly, makes The Undead Pool so extra special and worthy of being crowned THE BOOK of all Hollows books? Let's start with the plot. As usual, Rachel and company have a crisis on their hands, and this time around, it all starts with an exploding golf ball. Magic is on the fritz all across the city, with even the simplest and most innocent of charms turning deadly, and it's not picky about who it hurts, either. Anyone who is anyone in the Hollows world is affected or involved in some way. The danger is everywhere, striking hard and fast and never in the same place twice. Needless to say, tensions are high and tempers are short as everyone scrambles to figure out what's causing the magical mishaps and how to stop them - and naturally, right in the thick of the trouble is our favorite itchy witch, Rachel Morgan. <br /><br />I loved how big The Undead Pool was, and I'm not talking about the number of pages. Elves, demons, vampires, Weres, the FIB and the IS - they were all there and accounted for. Only the witches were missing, and with so many other peeps involved, I barely noticed their absence. You'd think that with such a diverse cast, the book would feel overcrowded, but Kim expertly juggles all the different characters and groups, giving each a vital role to play in the story without the story itself feeling weighed down or cluttered. What's more, she doesn't skip a single beat while doing it. The book's pacing never falters, the writing is as smooth as ever, and there's a perfect balance struck between riveting action scenes and quieter "human" moments. <br /><br />There's incredible character development as well. After twelve books, it's impossible for any reader not to become attached, and I'm no exception. I am terribly invested in the lives of Rachel, Ivy, Jenks, Trent, Al, Newt, David, Bis, Edden and everyone else who strides through the pages of the Hollows books. They've all come such a long way since the series started, and they continue to flourish in The Undead Pool. Rachel in particular has matured as a character, no longer recklessly rushing off on her own, straight into the arms of danger. She's impacted so many lives, and you really feel that in this book when everyone comes out of the woodwork to help her. Ivy has changed, too. She's still struggling to be her own vampire, but she's found love at last and even if she has to fight tooth and nail for it (which she does), she's more at peace than I have ever seen her. Or how about Trent, the once-murdering drug lord who has slowly but surely become a trusted friend, ally, and a hero worthy of the name? <br /><br />Now, you may have noticed I haven't said anything about romance. There's been one brewing for a while now, and the burning question on all of our minds is, "Will they or won't they?!" We're <i>aching</i> to find out if Rachel will get her HEA, and we've got very definite opinions about who she should get her HEA with. And that, my friends, is why The Undead Pool is THE BOOK. After what seems like the longest romantic draught in literary history, Rachel's love life finally gets some attention. As for what happens, and who it happens with.....you don't really expect me to tell you, do you? C'mon now, you know me better than that! But trust me, it's absolutely, positively worth all the years of waiting. <br /><br />There is so much more I could say and a thousand more praises I could sing about this book, because it's just that good. I've read it twice now and I'm still finding new bits to highlight and bookmark. Pretty soon my entire copy will be marked up, and you know what? I'm totally okay with that. <br /><br />The Undead Pool is another gripping Hollows adventure that is guaranteed to thrill and enchant fans, and I predict many (if not all) will end the book in a euphoric daze, their faces wreathed in smiles and their minds whirling as they try to process the sheer awesomeness of what they just read. Or maybe that's just me ;). <br /><br /><br />5 Stars ★★★★★<br /><br />ARC provided by the publisher in exchange for an honest review.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9230355293829136588" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer694318469" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13237197218260882465">Review also published at <a href='http://mybookshelfisready.tumblr.com/post/83740159432/the-undead-pool-by-kim-harrison' rel='nofollow noopener'>My Bookshelf is Ready</a>.<br/><br/>Okay, so basically a bunch of mystics find Rachel and make her a Goddess or something?? Harrison's often choppy writing style can be a bit hard to follow sometimes, so that bit was unclear. Anyway, Newt pulls them out and I guess puts them in a jar because they look like fireflies. Meh.<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394495145i/8860697.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Now, I'm not really a fan of romance in books but I'm guessing the people who were 'shipping Rachel and Trent will be excited that they finally hook up</span></span>
  <span id="freeText13237197218260882465" style="display:none">Review also published at <a href="http://mybookshelfisready.tumblr.com/post/83740159432/the-undead-pool-by-kim-harrison" rel="nofollow noopener">My Bookshelf is Ready</a>.<br><br>Okay, so basically a bunch of mystics find Rachel and make her a Goddess or something?? Harrison's often choppy writing style can be a bit hard to follow sometimes, so that bit was unclear. Anyway, Newt pulls them out and I guess puts them in a jar because they look like fireflies. Meh.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394495145i/8860697.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Now, I'm not really a fan of romance in books but I'm guessing the people who were 'shipping Rachel and Trent will be excited that they finally hook up in this one. It's been leaning toward this pairing for a few books now so it's really no surprise. What is disappointing is how big a deal they make elf sex out to be, and what actually happens is some of the most vanilla sex out there. They kinda do it on a table, then the couch. [Deadpan]: "Alert the church elders." There isn't even any foreplay. What's up with that?<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394495145ra/8860698.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Harrison is setting up for a finale which I think may be kinda lackluster. There will be some political and religious troubles with the elves and Ellasbeth up against Trent, who is losing his material power. I'm pretty sure Jenks is gonna die, just 'cuz. There's still this business of Rachel fixing Ivy's soul or whatever trope stolen from Buffy. Is Rachel out of a job? Because I don't remember her doing many runs in the last few books so there's also that. Al is pissed at Rachel because he had feelz for her and then she went and slept with Trent. Also, pretty sure that Trent and Rachel are going to have a kid because of the fixed genes blah blah blah. And surprise, surprise: Newt isn't all that crazy after all. There's just a lot of loose ends that the author has to clean up for the last book at this point.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_589614351" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/589614351" />
    <a title="Christal (Badass Book Reviews)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1180557-christal-badass-book-reviews"><img alt="Christal (Badass Book Reviews)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347376095p2/1180557.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/589614351?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christal (Badass Book Reviews)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christal (Badass Book Reviews)" href="/user/show/1180557-christal-badass-book-reviews">Christal (Badass Book Reviews)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1180557-christal-badass-book-reviews?shelf=weres-and-shifters">weres-and-shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1180557-christal-badass-book-reviews?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1180557-christal-badass-book-reviews?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1180557-christal-badass-book-reviews?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1180557-christal-badass-book-reviews?shelf=demons">demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1180557-christal-badass-book-reviews?shelf=fae">fae</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1180557-christal-badass-book-reviews?shelf=female-lead">female-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1180557-christal-badass-book-reviews?shelf=witches-warlocks-and-mages">witches-warlocks-and-mages</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1180557-christal-badass-book-reviews?shelf=gods-and-goddesses">gods-and-goddesses</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1180557-christal-badass-book-reviews?shelf=pi-detective-cop">pi-detective-cop</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer589614351" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15598553693294548041"><i>AH and I had a great <a href='http://badassbookreviews.com/early-group-review-the-undead-pool-by-kim-harrison/' rel='nofollow noopener'>group discussion</a> about this book over on <a href='http://badassbookreviews.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Badass Book Reviews</a>!</i><br/><br/><b>The Undead Pool</b> was another five-star read from Kim Harrison for me! I don't think this was my favorite book in the series but it was undeniably strong and presented some really interesting developments in Rachel's personal life.<br/><br/>Rachel has definitely grown and matured in this series. In <strong>The Undead Pool</strong>, Rachel has to figure out why spells are backfiring in The Hollows and how the chaos relates to her ley line. Rach</span>
  <span id="freeText15598553693294548041" style="display:none"><i>AH and I had a great <a href="http://badassbookreviews.com/early-group-review-the-undead-pool-by-kim-harrison/" rel="nofollow noopener">group discussion</a> about this book over on <a href="http://badassbookreviews.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Badass Book Reviews</a>!</i><br /><br /><b>The Undead Pool</b> was another five-star read from Kim Harrison for me! I don't think this was my favorite book in the series but it was undeniably strong and presented some really interesting developments in Rachel's personal life.<br /><br />Rachel has definitely grown and matured in this series. In <strong>The Undead Pool</strong>, Rachel has to figure out why spells are backfiring in The Hollows and how the chaos relates to her ley line. Rachel has really become a pivot point in Inderlander society and a lightening rod for change. Because of who and what she is, she's stirred up a lot of feelings between the elves and the demons.<br /><br />Speaking of elves and demons, this book is very strong in the Rachel/Trent force. I loved the developments in their relationship and I am eager to see how they proceed in the next book. I've always loved Rachel of course, but Trent was not my favorite character starting out. I was wary as he and Rachel started working together more and more, but now I love that he is in her life. Kim Harrison wrote a masterful slow play with his character.<br /><br />Jenks was his usual hilarious, yet insightful self. He really is one of the best "sidekicks" being written today. Ivy has become much stronger in her sense of self since the beginning of the series. Nina coming into her life has been good for her and I think she and Rachel are finally at a very healthy place in their friendship for both of them. Al wasn't around for much of this book and he was sorely missed. There is a heartbreaking scene between him and Rachel near the end of <b>The Undead Pool</b>, and I just hope that we see them make up in the next book. It might take a lot of cookies though... Ellasbeth and Jonathan were their usual terrible selves, but I do think there is more to Jonathan than we have seen so far. David and the pack actually go through a lot in this book and show that they can be powerful players in Inderland society.<br /><br />There were a lot of suprising reveals from Newt and Rachel learned even more about the origins of magic, but of course Kim Harrison isn't done with us yet. <strong>The Undead Pool</strong> represented a lot of changes for Rachel and Co., but I loved every minute of it! This book set into motion the events that will wrap up the series and, though I'll be sad to lose these characters, I can't wait to see what epic conclusion is in store for <em>The Hollows</em>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15598553693294548041" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1138678123" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1138678123" />
    <a title="Melliane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3166645-melliane"><img alt="Melliane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1309601809p2/3166645.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1138678123?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melliane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melliane" href="/user/show/3166645-melliane">Melliane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1138678123" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9423512556252715063"><a href='http://www.betweendandr.com/2015/05/31/the-undead-pool-de-kim-harrison-vo/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mon avis en Français</a><br/><br/><a href='http://www.betweendandr.com/2015/05/31/the-undead-pool-by-kim-harrison/' rel='nofollow noopener'>My English review</a><br/><br/>And here’s volume 12 and the countdown begins, yes, because the end is now very soon with the next and final volume. I am so sad to see the end approaching that fast but it does not change the fact that I once again had a great time with this adventure.<br/><br/>Our beloved heroine is as always very good at finding trouble and this time will not change that fact. Indeed, it seems that a wave of energy is following Rachel, causing the backfire of many charms causing ter</span>
  <span id="freeText9423512556252715063" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.betweendandr.com/2015/05/31/the-undead-pool-de-kim-harrison-vo/" rel="nofollow noopener">Mon avis en Français</a><br /><br /><a href="http://www.betweendandr.com/2015/05/31/the-undead-pool-by-kim-harrison/" rel="nofollow noopener">My English review</a><br /><br />And here’s volume 12 and the countdown begins, yes, because the end is now very soon with the next and final volume. I am so sad to see the end approaching that fast but it does not change the fact that I once again had a great time with this adventure.<br /><br />Our beloved heroine is as always very good at finding trouble and this time will not change that fact. Indeed, it seems that a wave of energy is following Rachel, causing the backfire of many charms causing terrible consequences for the many people who operate them. But this new phenomenon is much more than that because it seems that all masters vampires are plunged into an endless sleep and if it does not end quickly, it could cause their death. As always, Rachel will have to try to understand what is happening and to ally with her friends to save their town from a massive carnage. So our heroine will have to manage Trent and her feelings for him, but also Nina and Ivy, and all the problems that are happening in town. But nothing will be easy and even though some stories will evolve much more than what we thought, Rachel does not emerge unscathed.<br /><br />As I said, I had a great time with this story. We go through different states throughout the chapters. Oh yes, because Rachel is more and more aware of her feelings for Trent, those she was trying to forget so far. And yet she knows that even if she likes him, nothing is possible between them and she refuses to be the second woman. It must be one that he needs to lead his people, and he must be a good father to Lucy as well as a husband to his ex-fiancée. But can they ignore their feelings? To what price? I was really sad for Rachel, seeing that she was trying to resist as she understood how to act. Then, I must say that Trent does not help much either for that. I was also very surprised over the development with Al … I admit that I am still in shock and I wonder how it all will evolve or change … It really broke my heart me to see it all. We also learn more about the beliefs of the elves and about this goddess we hear so much about. Yes Rachel will have enough to do in this novel, and she will not have a second for her.<br /><br />One thing is sure, many things have begun here, good and bad ones, and the consequences are beginning to fall on our characters and I’m very curious to see what the author will provide us for the last book now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9423512556252715063" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_644459521" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/644459521" />
    <a title="Kira" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7247640-kira"><img alt="Kira" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1395614362p2/7247640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/644459521?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kira" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kira" href="/user/show/7247640-kira">Kira</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7247640-kira?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7247640-kira?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7247640-kira?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7247640-kira?shelf=demons">demons</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer644459521" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4348750263557870213">This book is everything I always wanted the series to be. Rachel matured. No more stupidly mouthing off and no more pointlessly running head first into danger. Rachel’s always going to be in danger but it’s better when she’s smart about it. I’ve always been a fan of Trent. He was cruel in the beginning but I felt like there was more to him. I love it when he and Rachel work together. They’re perfect for each other.<br/><br/>All hell is about to break loose since the master vampires are asleep. Of course i</span>
  <span id="freeText4348750263557870213" style="display:none">This book is everything I always wanted the series to be. Rachel matured. No more stupidly mouthing off and no more pointlessly running head first into danger. Rachel’s always going to be in danger but it’s better when she’s smart about it. I’ve always been a fan of Trent. He was cruel in the beginning but I felt like there was more to him. I love it when he and Rachel work together. They’re perfect for each other.<br /><br />All hell is about to break loose since the master vampires are asleep. Of course it’s up to Rachel to save everyone. The vampires weren’t in this too much, which I was grateful for. They irritate the hell out of me. I wish the demons had been in it more. Even though Al was an ass, every moment with him was great. Newt stole the show. She may be crazy as hell but she’s smart and interesting. <br /><br />Elves sure are arrogant. Trent is despite his change in circumstances. Ellasbeth expects everything to go according to her whims. After learning about their goddess, it makes sense because she’s pretty damn arrogant too. I liked learning more about the elves and demons although I feel like there is still a lot more that we don’t know. The elven magic storyline wasn’t my favorite, but everything else about the book made up for it. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4348750263557870213" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('aB/yhuHq+8Vgj9pAmpTZ/x82buK9zm0PzM8tcNP6RGWN51K3NDvvKcgjcl/m4dR0jYojnUfWI9sMo7fCENoRSg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('OqIjKNF4WH9b3E6Vh3V08fDkfbCtlvniveWdvaBiuFDfWoMZBKlMk/Nw5or7AHl6Ylgwz1eOtzZ9iQcPY0Ltfw==')})
  }
//]]>

  <span id="freeText1239414618831779853" style="display:none">Kim Harrison is best known as the author of the New York Times #1 best selling Hollows series, but she has written more than urban fantasy and has published over two-dozen books spanning the gamut from young adult, thriller, several anthologies, and has scripted two original graphic novels.       newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_8138071').observe('prototip:shown', function () {

              return;

            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });

            <span class="readable">&ldquo;His expression became serious, and his hand almost slipped from mine. "I've had a long time to think about it."<br /><br />"This can't work!"<br /><br />He looked down, then jerked his head up in frustration as his finger tightened on mine. "I'm not asking you to marry me, Rachel. I just ..."<br /><br />My heart pounded, and he stepped closer, so close the scent of cinnamon and wine enveloped me.<br /><br />"I like walking into a room and seeing your face light up when you see me," he said earnestly, the sun from the open window making his hair glow. "I like arguing with Quen over the wisdom of employing a demon to be my security."<br /><br />My throat caught. This wasn't going to happen, but something in me was withering. I wanted more--and I knew I couldn't have it.<br /><br />He touched my hair, and I twitched as he tucked a strand of hair behind my ear. “I want to wake up beside you, see your curls on my pillow. I want a chance at falling in love.” <br /><br />My breath came fast. That was what I wanted too, and it hurt more than I thought was possible to survive.&rdquo;</span>

I asked again, more stridently. <br /><br />Silent, he sat there, his hands on the wheel as he stared at the front door and the neon bowling pins flashing on and off. "I want it to be.&rdquo;</span>
